B00D6JX3OM|5.0|Sting's latest release, The Last Ship, is in his own words, both a memoir to his growing up in Wallsend, an English shipbuilding town, and a tribute to working class people in general.  It's also the basis for a play he's developing and a very personal, emotional and stirring album depicting a way of life that's coming to an end and its affect on the community.  From the romantic reminiscings of a street brawler wooing the love of his life, a man in love with a woman who doesn't love him to a son's rebellion against his father's wishes to follow in his footsteps taking up a dead end job because it's tradition- The Last Ship displays some amazing imagery and storytelling from a modern day master bard.  The music is mainly traditional English folk and shanty, even a jig & reel, incorporating all the styles and instrumentation- fiddles, penny whistles, accordians, bagpipes, bodhran drums, clog dancing, etc- you'd expect, especially in today's music landscape dominated with bands like Mumford & Sons.  But what's surprising is the assortment of guest appearances on the cd, including Jimmy Nail and AC/DC's Brian Johnson, of all people.<br /><br />Last Ship is a beautifully rendered, absolutely poetic project full of heart and humanity.  If the stage version lives up to the music, it'll really be something to see.

The translation is absolutely stunning, and is probably the truest to the actual words of the Hebrew and Greek texts on the market today.<br /><br />The buyer should be aware that the study materials and footnotes are written from a very conservative, Evangelical perspective for a very conservative, Evangelical audience. As a somewhat conservative mainline Protestant, there are a few contentions in the footnotes and supplementary texts that caused me to raise some eyebrows (see a footnote on page 65 for Genesis 9:5-6 that outright supports the death penalty), but nothing so serious as to detract from the outstanding quality of this work. For the most part, the accompanying material is relevant, engaging, and thought provoking (perhaps most of all because I may disagree with the editors on some points!)<br /><br />So to conclude, the ESV Study Bible should not scare away center-right, middle-of-the road or even moderately liberal mainline protestants. The clarity of its translation and faithfulness to the source texts is, for me, a welcome retreat from the NRSV, a translation which (particularly in the Old Testament) let political correctness wedge itself between the source text and the translation. The only folks who should avoid this are far-left of center Christians in any denomination. The lack of gender neutrality and the word-for-word translation methodology employed will undoubtedly bug you.

I think he would have been wise to realize that survivors of 9/11 and their families might not appreciate some sections of the book.<br /><br />I do not think that this is a return to form for him at all. Instead of finding this greatly anticipated novel a classic in his genre I found at times the subject matter to be revolting and offensive.  I don't think revolting and offensive is what we usually get with Stephen King, we usually get mind churning, 'don't look under the bed' creeps (often from mundane and seemingly harmless things or people) and that's what I read him for. The way he usually weaves his words is hypnotic and graceful.  I really don't know what happened in this book, it's harsh and lacks style. The first half of the book, for me at any rate, is so uncharacteristic I could hardly believe he'd written it.  The second part of the book does return to form in some sections, but it still feels to lack much of the incredible style so many of us have come to love.

1250007208|4.0|Cinder is one of those books that everyone really loved and raved about, so I knew I had to get my hands on a copy. Welp, I finally (I know!) read it and I have to say, I'm thoroughly glad I did. Not many books live up to the hype but this is certainly one of them. Cinderella wasn't exactly my favourite fairy tale but when you put a futuristic spin on it, suddenly, it becomes totally awesome!<br /><br />This book brings a fresh, new twist to fairy tale retellings with its heavy science fiction influence and incredible future-filled world building. You can definitely see the parallels between it and the original source material but the connections aren't so blatant that you're able to predict exactly where the story is going to end. That being said, there were a few big revelations regarding Cinder's true identity that I was able to pinpoint pretty early in, but overall, they didn't detract from my enjoyment of the book.<br /><br />There's a lot going on in Cinder --- androids, lunars, cyborgs, classism, intergalactic war --- but it's all woven together in a way that makes sense. And futhermore, there's the romance, familial relationships and friendships that bind it all together. Admittedly, I was more entranced by the Meyer's storytelling and compelling plot than I was by the actual characters which isn't to say they were bad, because they weren't. While I liked Cinder and Kai, they didn't captivate me in the way they seemed to do with everyone else. Instead, I was more interested in the book's secondary characters: Iko, Dr. Erland, Pearl, even Queen Levana. I guess I just didn't connect with the MC's as much as the others, though I did feel for their situations (equality struggles, political problems, etc.).<br /><br />Overall, I'd say Cinder was a fast-paced, fun read with a unique premise and culturally distinct setting which meshed so well with the book's futuristic vibe. What really intrigued me was Meyer's ability to add so much dimension to such a familiar tale by infusing so many diverse ideas into it. While I expected to engage a bit more with the MC's and though some of the surprises were anticipated, I wasn't at all disappointed. The book definitely lives up to the hype! I'm really excited to see how Meyer will weave this story into her next set of fairytales and am wondering exactly how they'll all manage to find their happily ever after.<br /><br />Food for Thought: Cinder is one of the few stories that actually lives up to all the hype. A little bit classic and a lot sci-fi, it puts a fresh spin on fairy tale retellings. Though I wasn't as taken with our MC as much as some of the others, this book is a fun, quick read that will entrance a whole new generation of fairy tale lovers with its incredible uniqueness and wonderful world building. B00DJZR46G|4.0|(A 21-track deluxe edition featuring two exclusive tracks is available only at Target.)<br /><br />The concept behind \\"The Diving Board,\\" Elton John's sophisticated new offering - his first solo outing since 2006's criminally underrated \\"The Captain and the Kid\\" - is one of simplicity, of intentionally harking back to the stark, literate sound he quietly descended upon downtown Los Angeles with in 1970 when he powerfully made his American debut at the Troubador.<br /><br />That alone makes it a worthy, often harrowing listen, though the songwriting itself is unquestionably ripened, wizened and mature in perspective - that John and lyricist Bernie Taupin are no longer the two lads who wrote \\"Your Song\\" and \\"The Greatest Discovery\\" is quite clear - making for an intriguing, if at first alarming, and not always successful, musical dichotomy.<br /><br />When Taupin is at his best it is something to behold. Lead single \\"Home Again,\\" the most radio-friendly tune among the dozen, is achingly beautiful and universal in its sentiments without a trace of treacle, beckoning one of John's most buttery, ingratiating melodies. \\"Oscar Wilde Gets Out\\" is as epic as one of his early 70s story songs, and John responds with a bone-chilling performance.<br /><br />\\"Oceans Away\\" is a classy, dignifying, and, above all, poetic tribute to the Greatest Generation and those they left behind in World War II. John's matter-of-fact, graceful vocal underscores the pathos and power of Taupin's key points, and his playing is arresting and rapturous.<br /><br />There are also moments where one cannot help but be reminded of Taupin's claim that he is writing lyrics now by and large as \\"a hobby.\\" While the results of songs such as \\"Mexican Vacation\\" and \\"A Town Called Jubilee\\" are certainly listenable, with John's piano obscuring some of their lesser qualities, they call no individual attention to themselves and are not memorable, with no huggably warm sounds to anchor them. In the past, such as on 1997's \\"The Big Picture,\\" John has been able to squeeze out juicy melodies to some of Taupin's worst lyrics, but on \\"The Diving Board,\\" where his once-in-a-lifetime way with a piano is front and center to achieve a certain sound, by necessity lessening the importance of melody, the lyrical shortcomings are more obvious, especially because John has long been keen to giftwrap Taupin's words, regardless of poetic worth, in maximally melodic packaging.<br /><br />Still, selections that impress and comfortably remind of previous majesty cannot be denied. Taupin's lyrics for \\"Voyeur\\" bring out the ever-adventurous side of John's pallette, with kinetic, undeniable energy. It is the kind of song that might have been compromised by the loud, overproduced atmosphere of albums like \\"The Big Picture\\" or 1992's otherwise powerful \\"The One.\\"<br /><br />\\"I'll come away with something to keep you in my heart,\\" John sings with uncommon passion before diving into a brazen, enchanting solo, the likes of which longtime listeners associate with albums such as \\"Goodbye Yellow Brick Road.\\"<br /><br />Furthermore, \\"The Diving Board\\" is anchored by three instrumental solos that, quite predictably, are marvelous and attention-seizing. The third of these, \\"Dream No. 3,\\" is easily one of the best moments of John's career, winding down into the loungey, bluesy title track.<br /><br />One unique trait of Sir Elton's is that his compound professionalism and genius as a musician has never eluded him, not even in periods where his life was at a particularly low ebb. The result is that he has never crafted an album without something wortwhile resulting - those mid-80s LPs may have had filler, but the gems, once found, were unquestionable. Similar can be said here, only this time the highlights are less radio-friendly, yet more plentiful and with more weight and substance, and now instead of personal demons creeping into the music he has two lovely young boys and a happy, healthy marriage which meaneven more to him than his career. That comfortability waves in some less than compelling moments into \\"The Diving Board\\" but is also its asset - relieved of the burden to find a hit single or cater to the casual listener, John presents himself with a take-it-or-leave-it attitude, making the gambles really count and giving the highlights extra grist.<br /><br />One does hope, however, that he will return to the atittude of 2001's \\"Songs from the West Coast.\\" Though more reined in than \\"The Diving Board,\\" it proved he could go back to the template of his classic albums without sacrificing those instantly memorable melodic hooks.even more to him than his career. B00DGGIXS6|4.0|Cher is never even the slightest bit phoney in an industry where phoney is the name of the game. That matter-of-fact generosity of spirit informs 2013's aptly-titled \\"Closer to the Truth\\" and makes it a more winning formula than it would be in the hands of a lesser vocalist. Her large, purple voice propels the songs, regardless of their intrinsic value, making her long awaited return a welcome one.<br /><br />While the album lacks the big, bursting energy of singles like \\"Strong Enough\\" and \\"Song for the Lonely,\\" tunes that beckoned repeated plays and airwave saturation, it has a more varied style of songs and a consistently higher quality of material. While the second half of the \\"Living Proof\\" album, for instance, contained smatterings of definite filler, with \\"Closer to the Truth\\" that is not the case. Each selection showcases a facet of Cher's outsized personality.<br /><br />The album is frontloaded with tunes ripe for the dance floor. Lead single \\"A Woman's World\\" is fluffy, infectious fun - when she cries out that she's \\"strong enough to rise above - this is a woman's world!\\" it's hard to do anything to believe her, the sentiment coming as it does from the mouth of a woman who seemingly survives all.<br /><br />\\"Take It Like a Man\\" featuring Jake Shears and the attitudinal \\"Dressed to Kill\\" also get the sweat dripping and the grooves flashing. Even though her delivery could perhaps benefit from a little more menace on the latter, her understatedness is also a statement in itself - with a track record like hers, what is there left to prove or question?<br /><br />\\"Lovers Forever,\\" which Cher co-pens, is arguably the best of the dance-pop selections, with its insistent, chugging and swirling synths. The up-and-down nature of the melody gives her singing ability a highly listenable workout. It's destined to fill dance floors and workout playlists.<br /><br />Of particular importance are \\"I Walk Alone,\\" \\"Red\\" and \\"Favorite Scars.\\" All three accent the niche she has carved with her extreme sustenance and longevity. \\"Red\\" in particular is a shot of grizzled, worldy-wise near-cynicism perfectly suited to Cher, anchored by a repetitive but catchy pop hook and anthem-sized production values. The mercurial \\"I Walk Alone,\\" one of two tracks co-penned by Pink, is tailored to Cher with its themes of independence and coming-of-age.<br /><br />The ballads, surprisingly, are what work best of all. Cher seemingly weaves gold from the rather formulaic \\"I Hope You Find It,\\" actually a Miley Cyrus cover, meaning it's finally getting sung by proper pipes. Though the emotions run a little treacly and the production, as on most of the album, is too heavy-handed, the results stand up because of Cher's bold vocals and investment in the lyrical content. Time has simply not weathered her instrument.<br /><br />\\"Sirens\\" is certainly the album's most valuable moment. Her earnest, precise execution of the soul-bearing lyrics affords the listener a look into her remarkably large heart. She sounds both vulnerable and dazzling - a better rendering of the song does not seem possible.<br /><br />It was a long, long time in coming, but \\"Closer to the Truth\\" is finally here, and it's a definite pleasure. The third of these, \\"Dream No. 3,\\" is easily one of the best moments of John's career, winding down into the loungey, bluesy title track.<br /><br />One unique trait of Sir Elton's is that his compound professionalism and genius as a musician has never eluded him, not even in periods where his life was at a particularly low ebb. The result is that he has never crafted an album without something wortwhile resulting - those mid-80s LPs may have had filler, but the gems, once found, were unquestionable. Similar can be said here, only this time the highlights are less radio-friendly, yet more plentiful and with more weight and substance, and now instead of personal demons creeping into the music he has two lovely young boys and a happy, healthy marriage which mean even more to him than his career. That comfortability waves in some less than compelling moments into \\"The Diving Board\\" but is also its asset - relieved of the burden to find a hit single or cater to the casual listener, John presents himself with a take-it-or-leave-it attitude, making the gambles really count and giving the highlights extra grist.<br /><br />One does hope, however, that he will return to the atittude of 2001's \\"Songs from the West Coast.\\" Though more reined in than \\"The Diving Board,\\" it proved he could go back to the template of his classic albums without sacrificing those instantly memorable melodic hooks.<br /><br />(A 21-track deluxe edition featuring two exclusive tracks is available only at Target.)t more plentiful and with more weight and substance, and now instead of personal demons creeping into the music he has two lovely young boys and a happy, healthy marriage which mean even more to him than his career. B00DJZR46G|5.0|The narrative around Elton John's new album \\"Diving Board\\" is about a return to a stripped down, sparse piano and lyric-driven sensibility of his early days. Go back to 2001 and the same claims were also being made for the excellent \\"Songs from the West Coast\\". But on this album Elton John has again enlisted the producing \\"gun for hire\\" T Bone Burnett, fresh from work with Diana Krall, Steve Earle, Gregg Allman and of course rekindling the link with Elton forged on 2011's \\"The Union\\".<br /><br />The Burnett and John link up adds new dimensions not least with Bernie Taupin firing on all lyrical cylinders and the producer essentially dismissing band support. The result is that \\"The Diving Board\\" is a fine album recalling the wonders of the early Elton which got lost over the years in \\"Tantrums and Tiaras\\". So it back to a proper emphasis on songs and all the better for it. Opener \\"Oceans Away\\" sets the tone with Elton singing better than ever as and where he opens with the confession that \\"I hung out with the old folks/ in the hope that I'd get wise/I was trying to bridge the gap, between the great divide\\". Other great songs follow not least the haunting \\"Town called jubilee\\" and the brilliant standout \\"My Quicksand\\" which is one of the better songs he has written in years. The album is punctuated with 3 \\"Dream\\" piano interludes and the sumptuous third of these is also Keith Jarrett like in composition.<br /><br />Songs like \\"Can I stay alone tonight\\" hark back to that vintage era of \\"Tumbleweed Connection\\" as does the splendid \\"Take This Dirty Water\\" where Elton sings sagely \\"If you break some bones on landing/ You'll know you're built to last\\". It is three of the darker songs here however which impress most. \\"Oscar Wilde gets out\\" charting the writers sad departure to France post Reading Jail is an automatic start for downloads. The \\"New Fever Waltz\\" would not go amiss on a Tom Waits album while the highly reflective almost Randy Newman style song \\"Home Again\\" is pure class.<br /><br />\\"The Diving Board\\" is a master class in song writing and sees Elton John at his most intimate and introspective. Perhaps it is not sardine packed with obvious hits but taken as a whole it is his most solid and worthwhile album in a decade. The old Rocket Man has got back into groove, and achieved lift off. Part of this stems from the fact that he is clearly enjoying himself greatly not least on the evidence of \\"Mexican Vacation (Kids in Candlelight)\\" and the excellent bluesy title track. This reviewer would not claim to be a fully paid up member of the Elton John fan club but this is one record of his that you really need.re class.<br /><br />\\"The Diving Board\\" is a master class in song writing and sees Elton John at his most intimate and introspective. B00D3LA5WG|4.0|Note: May contain spoilers. Proceed with caution.<br /><br />When looking at a film like Mud it's hard to picture Matthew McConaughey being fit to play the titular character. Sure, he's had a handful of serious roles in the past, but majority of his work consists of Rom-Coms and things of that nature. However, it's this odd casting choice that makes Mud such a surprise hit. Not only is McConaughey able to pull of this role, but he does it with such ease that you would think he gets offered roles like this all the time. With that said, though, Mud is such a unique film that even McConaughey's stellar performance feels like a minor element in a much bigger picture.<br /><br />There's no denying that Mud's title and marketing are a bit misleading. While the story does center around the titular Mud, he isn't necessarily the main character of the film. No, that titled is reserved for a young boy named Ellis (Tye Sheridan). Living in De Witt, Arkansas with his friend Neckbone (Jacob Lofland), the two boys come across a presumably deserted island while riding their boat one morning. However, it doesn't take long before they come across a man named Mud. After sharing his story with the boys, they learn that he is trying to reunite with his childhood sweetheart Juniper (Reese Witherspoon), but is on the run from some bounty hunters and needs their help.<br /><br />One of Mud's strongest attributes is its cast and their performances, but the story's purity and unpredictability are what really connected with me. Because of this, there's no way to gain a real understanding of the story based on the brief synopsis provided above or on the back of the box. At its core, Mud is about a young boy's crippled understanding of love. Ellis believes that if two people love each other then they should be together, but everywhere he turns another relationship is crumbling. Whether its his parents marriage, the complicated relationship between Mud and Juniper, or his horrible experience with his first \\"girlfriend\\", Ellis' faith in true love slowly deteriorates as the film progresses and its almost heartbreaking to watch.<br /><br />As a result, Mud's character progression makes itself known throughout the entirety of the film. Not only from Ellis, but from Mud as well. By the time you reach the story's conclusion you see drastic change in both of these characters and its arguably the result of them meeting each other. Ellis is no longer the naive boy blindly living in an imperfect world and Mud is finally able to move on and do the right thing for both himself and those around him. The viewer also sees a slight change in both Neckbone and Senior (Ray McKinnon), Ellis' father, but their growth isn't as apparent as the two leads.<br /><br />Mud's casting is something that's been praised quite a bit by those who have seen the film, and for good reason. Not only were the actors perfect for their roles, but everyone involved did a phenomenal job of bringing these characters to life. Sheridan and McConaughey are bound to leave the biggest impression due to them receiving the most screen time, but it would be wrong to ignore the fact that Witherspoon, Lofland, McKinnon and Sam Shepard all delivered outstanding performances as well. While I would have liked to see more emphasis put on some of the characters like Juniper and Tom, it's no small feat that even the minor performances stood out as much as they did.<br /><br />Finally, the film's sense of atmosphere is outstanding. Part of this is brought out by the cast's performances, but it's also accomplished through the film's score, composed by David Wingo. Both of these elements combined really help bring to life the gritty southern setting. David's compositions are dark, ominous, and, at times, even a little thrilling. They're a perfect fit for the story being told and without them there's no arguing that the film wouldn't be nearly as enjoyable.<br /><br />Overall Score: 8/10 - Among other things, Mud is powerful and confident. The story is engaging, the setting is raw, and it's all tied together with some fantastic performances and an equally enjoyable score. However, all of these things are just small parts of a greater whole and that's what helps make Mud feel like a cohesive experience. If you had your eye on this before I definitely recommend you give it your time. It easily exceeded my expectations.

B00DRGQZRG|5.0|In spite of the hype, this is not a fusion album. The days of swirling organs, acid-inflected screaming guitars, and blustery drums mixed with exotic substances, inner enlightenment, and science fiction crossovers are dead and gone. Please listen to this album as simply a 2013 electric jazz set.<br /><br />The fusion rumors surfaced when people noticed that for the first time in decades, a Dave Holland-led album did not feature any trumpets, saxes, or trombones, nor was it a big band album. While there are references to past ensembles and recordings (such as Holland's 1990 Extensions album, or Eubanks' 1992 Turning Point album), Prism is something radically different and new, and at 70:07 will repay many years of listening.<br /><br />With Craig Taborn on piano and Fender Rhodes, Kevin Eubanks on guitars, and Eric Harland on drums, there is plenty of soloing for everyone, yet no one dominates. Wait until you hear Eubanks' twisted, distorted lines on \\"The Watcher\\", the Leslie-cabinet effect on \\"Choir\\", the Gibson hollow-body sound on the spooky \\"The Color of Iris\\", and the Wah-Wah pedal on \\"Breathe\\". More than just a non-stop soloist, he often doubles the melody lines with Taborn. Eric Harland is quite simply amazing, especially in a rimshot solo at the end of \\"Evolution\\". Taborn is the \\"most free\\" of this incomparable quartet: the quirky stops and starts of \\"Spirals\\" and the towering solos he plays on \\"The True Meaning of Determination\\" and \\"Evolution\\" are awe-inspiring.<br /><br />And what of Holland himself? As always, he's the bedrock beneath the terra firma. His all-too-rare solos sound so effortless that they almost defer attention. In spite of throwing jabs like a heavyweight champ, the listener can almost take his lines for granted, so cohesively do they mesh into the musical fabric. And while no one would compare this album to 1978's all-solo Emerald Tears, his dexterity, innovation, and virtuosity have not suffered after almost 50 years of recorded performances. For all those interested in the players involved, this purchase is what is colloquially known as a \\"no-brainer\\".

In part, they're right to do so; the film, like the second, wastes a lot of its potential with a third-act twist that (let's face it) is rather predictable.  BUT, unlike the second film, it at least tries to do something else.  I won't say what, but it's nice to see a blockbuster shy away from conventional expectations.  That being said...it IS still a letdown, albeit one boasted by some great performances (Kingsley in particular, but Guy Pearce has a few good moments as well, and James Badge Dale has some nice scenes).  Rebecca Hall gets little to do, but she does it well; same with returning stars Gwyneth Paltrow, Don Cheadle, and Jon Favreau.<br /><br />Ultimately, how you feel about IRON MAN 3 will come down to your expectations going into it.  If you keep your expectations realistic (remember: IRON MAN 2), then you may be pleasantly surprised...unless you're fiercely loyal to the source material, in which case you're gonna be disappointed.  IRON MAN 3 isn't the film it could have been, but that's actually a two-way street: it could have been better, but could have been much worse.  Take that for what you will, but at least it's another chance for Robert Downey Jr. to quip some one-liners and give the cameras a mischievous glare.Don Cheadle, and Jon Favreau.<br /><br />Ultimately, how you feel about IRON MAN 3 will come down to your expectations going into it. 1476727651|4.0|The return-to-form King displayed with 11/22/63 and the novella JOYLAND continues for the most part with King's long-awaited 36-years-later sequel to 1977's THE SHINING.  Picking up only a few years after the conclusion of events in THE SHINING, the prologue features one of the most memorable apparitions from The Overlook making a welcome return &#34;haunting&#34;. From there, the novel jumps ahead a couple of decades, picking up with Danny at his lowest point in his late twenties before coursing ahead several more years. The pacing is a little disjointed at times and I was disappointed that some of Dan's arguably more compelling years (his teenage years) - and characters such as Wendy and Dick Hallorann - are never really explored to the extent or depth I had hoped they would be. A little more detail and padding here would have been welcome. However, King has often been criticized for his meandering, overlong style so many readers may relish this slightly more concise style.  The constant references throughout to even minor events in THE SHINING will have most readers inevitably comparing it to the earlier book (throwbacks to &#34;REDRUM&#34; and many other references abound). While DOCTOR SLEEP does work as a stand-alone novel, it works best as a sequel. There are two main threads to this novel: the exploration and expansion of the character of the now adult 'Doc', as he battles with his demons (alcoholism, his past, and his shining ability); and the new story and characters such as Abra, Chetta, Lucy, Doctor John, Dave, and The True Knot. The new characters, especially Abra, are well drawn but the villains come across as a little hammy and the overall plot pales in comparison to Dan's inner ruminations.  The book's strongest point is the characterization of the original character and his expansion, with the main plot (new characters, new villains) being somewhat weaker but serviceable. As is typical with many King novels, the ending is a bit of a letdown - (smallspoiler) it's not bad but it is a little predictable and the final showdown is rushed with its infamous Colorado setting underused.  King says that this novel is a &#34;return to balls-to-the-wall, keep-the-lights-on scary horror&#34; and eerie early scenes in the prologue and when Dan's Shining returns with a bang in Teenytown seem to promise this, but it never really manifests, and overall the novel is not at all scary or even particularly creepy. Unfortunately, while it is suspenseful, much of the tale is just not as compelling or terrifying as it could have been. It's more of a supernatural adventure than a horror - an enjoyable and entertaining adventure for the most part that also serves as a poignant story of redemption, exploring themes such as mortality, family, and second chances.  Due to high expectations, you may be disappointed - don't expect a direct sequel to THE SHINING, but view it more as a continuation of the character of Dan with a new story and lots of references to the original novel. Don't expect a horror novel either - view this as more of a supernatural adventure crossed with a poignant story of redemption. It's far from perfect (few sequels are) and it's not better than the original, but it does continue the tale of Dan Torrance in an effective and heartfelt manner, features a good (though not great) premise, and introduces some interesting new characters, while also being respectful of and paying homage to its roots. Despite its flaws, DOCTOR SLEEP is a solid work.

B00D1QBQ2G|5.0|This album's subject matter is about the first, most scandalous pop culture star of the Italian settecento. The print media described Caffarelli as vicious as Farinelli was virtuous. He had an infectious personality that ignited scuffles, duels, and angry husbands on his hunt for blood. His histrionics on and off the stage went as far as heckling, mocking, and disrupting his fellow singers while on scene. He was boastful about his earnings, and emphasized how much more money he made than anyone else.  Though some critics and composers declared him superior to Farinelli, in the final analysis, Caffarelli did not go down into posterity as the best singer. He was persistent to alienate those who influence judgment about him at the peak of his career.<br /><br />To speak of this album, a word or two also needs to be said about Franco, the artist and the singer.<br /><br />As the singer, he has a before and after delineated by his 2012 Leonardo Vinci's Arbace.<br /><br />His before as a countertenor is relatively obscure, and frankly it does not matter quite more. Since Vo Solcando, he climbed to prominence and now flies high. Comparison between him and the other countertenors cannot be ignored as either he set himself apart as a mezzo or just raised the bar a lot higher for other countertenors. For now, he is in a league of his own.<br /><br />While most other artists are waging the grand battle of Son Qual Naves among themselves, it is refreshing Franco obliged to suppress it because, well, this is a Caffarelli tribute after all. It is also welcome that worn-out repertoire like Ombra mai fu and Scherza infida were clich&eacute;d out...and by the way, Son qual nave is a great aria which has become de rigueur just like lawyers having to pass the BAR exam to start practicing.<br /><br />The album's melancholic arias are sublime, and impossible for a foul creature, like Cafarelli was painted, to have inspired such finesse of the soul. Go figure. Franco sings these largos in almost a transcendental, timeless pathos with all nuance of nostalgia. Some scores could have the uncanny factor of period museum pieces; however, Franco interprets them in a form that grips attention and excitement. The result is worth his effort and risk taken here.<br /><br />As the artist, Franco creates a well conceptualized vocal portrait of Caffarelli. The collection of arias is cohesive yet with enough diversity in the vocal line to showcase the style and skills that Caffarelli could have been known for. The album's mix of new with known music shows great taste, and forethought to please the fans, not just the academic cognescenti. The orchestration of the arias de agilita share common elements in the use of horns and timpani, instruments reserved for the role of God or gods by baroque convention. Since these Caffarelli roles were neither, it is plausible that he imposed these musical requirements to please his own sense of grandiosity. This album is the best retrospective of a castrato made to date.<br /><br />With the opening aria, Fra l'orror della tempesta, Franco pays the price of admission as a baroque singer with his masterful execution of the vocal runs. They are furious, completed in one single breath, and adorned with double trills, martellos, and ringing tones which are now his signature. The melismatic movements ending in \\"tempesta\\" are inflected to sound like the strong gusts of a storm while the ones ending in \\"scintillar\\" have a brighter and more acute tone foretelling a glimmer of hope in the eye of the storm. The remaining lyrics are strung together in rapid staccato that flows with the fast unrelenting continuo that turns this entire aria into an instrumental allegro di molto.<br /><br />The promotional video on YouTube appears to be a little light-hearted showing Franco mentoring his own orchestra director. Humor aside, their timing is mercurial in coupling horn fortissimos with martellos to produce the effect of two vocal bombas in Fral'orror, and in highlighting Franco's ringing tones with sudden pops of violin obligato.<br /><br />Considering the complexity of this repertoire, and the skill used to hone its past glory, one can reasonably think that Franco is unto something very special when vocal painting the castrato artistry. His re-creation is credible. He made art. I dig it, and look forward to more.of violin obligato.    Considering the complexity of this repertoire, and the skill used to hone its past glory, one can reasonably think that Franco is unto something very special when vocal painting the castrato artistry. His re-creation is credible. He made art. I dig it, and look forward to more.

'Scenes from a Nights Dream' - Nice mix, vocals really come thru.  'Down and Out' is vibrant, drums sound amazing.  Overall, I could live with this copy. I prefer the orginal 1980 mix, where Phil & Tony are more or less equal and balanced.  Now here is an ODD one.  Visually, 'Man of our Times' looks completely different based on the grooves. Trick was warped, and Wind had pressing/cutting issues on side 2.  Duke is passable and Abacab and Three could be consider keepers -vs- old worn out vinyl.<br /><br />Part of me wonders if these vinyl recordings didn't go from Analog to Digital to Analog instead of true Analog from start to finish. B00E6890VC|5.0|Probably the most anticipated debut album since \\"Manners\\" from Passion Pit, Glasgow band CHVRCHES (pronounced Churches) has finally released \\"Bones of What You Believe\\" to the masses! CHVRCHES has already made four singles available to the public, but how does the rest of the album stand up? Pretty well to be honest.<br /><br />After a couple of listens, what stands out the most is Lauren Mayberry's beautifully sonic and wide ranging vocals. Some bands have lead singers that tend to clash with the instrumentation; not in this case though as Lauren's voice thankfully compliments everything that plays in the background. Synths pulse and pop from the get-go up until the final gorgeous ballad of \\"You Caught the Light\\". It is a very infectious tune and it is obvious that the band took a lot of inspiration from 80's music of yesteryear.<br /><br />\\"Gun\\" is their catchiest song and the entire track has that addictive 80's vibe that is difficult to mistake. \\"Tether\\" is an ambitious slow paced piece (at least compared to the rest of the album) that has a stellar two minute finale as synths blare in the background and Lauren's vocals become intertwined with the music. \\"Lungs\\", with it's teenage sugary sweetness, is another brilliant melodious track that sounds like it would be meant for a high school play, and \\"You Caught the Light\\" is a fantastic slow-moving closing song that ties up everything nicely with optimism and joy.<br /><br />Though the synths and vocals are memorable, the actual lyrical content is the weakest part of the album and a tad simplistic for my liking. There are dark themes of broken relationships, abuse and acts of revenge, but nothing that delves too deep into the subconscious. Perhaps the band was attempting to do what Foster the People did in \\"Pumped Up Kicks\\" and combine ominous lyrics with a catchy distracting beat. To be honest though, CHVRCHES is not quite as successful in accomplishing this feat. It is also worth mentioning that the band can be explicit sometimes as Lauren throws the f-word once into every other song. It does not go against the music, and is fairly sporadic, but it is there in case you are worried about swearing.<br /><br />All in all, \\"Bones of What You Believe\\" is a fantastic debut album by new players CHVRCHES. As noted before, the lyrics are not as deep as something you would find from Passion Pit or Foster the People, but the music is infectious and catchy! It is simple but effective, and the melody does it's job very very well. Cheers to CHVRHCES and I look forward to hearing more from them in the future!<br /><br />Rating: 4.5/5 Stars<br />Best Songs: \\"Gun\\", \\"Tether\\", \\"Lungs\\" & \\"You Caught the Light\\"

B00D6DVSAE|4.0|This album represents another in a long line of new directions for Sting -- show tunes, many of them acoustic and many sung in the Geordi accent of Sting's native Newcastle area. There is a strong sense of narrative as these songs come, apparently, from a forthcoming stage production. A lot of the music is wistful and melancholy, and much of it has strong Celtic overtones that give it an Irish-like feel.<br /><br />This is a good album and rates a solid four stars, with a qualification: If you're not already a Sting fan, I doubt you'll be converted by this one. But if you are the kind of a fan who gets into deep cuts and not just the \\"greatest hits\\", you may like it a lot. This album does not necessarily deliver immediate gratification, but will be worthwhile for fans patient enough to invest some time with it.<br /><br />In refreshingly disarming liner notes, Sting is up front about the fact that this album revisits the themes of the dying shipyards from Newcastle that provided the metaphorical backdrop for his album [[ASIN:B000002GL2 The Soul Cages]], a reaction to his own father's death. Sting describes The Soul Cages as \\"the least loved, least understood of all my recorded efforts\\". This time, rather than a sprawling New Age meditation on death, we have Celtic-inspired sounds, some quite rousing, many others quite lovely.<br /><br />After a couple of listens, I'm not hearing an obvious hit single here, which is in a way kind of refreshing for Sting. It is a solid album and seems to me designed to be listened to as an overall album rather than a collection of songs. The overall effect is pretty cohesive and pleasant, despite the sometimes peculiar, affected-sounding accents.<br /><br />In terms of comparison to Sting's earlier work, does anyone remember his \\"Mack the Knife\\" from the Kurt Weill tribute album [[ASIN:B000002GH2 Lost in the Stars]]? That what this reminded me of most -- largely acoustic with an old-fashioned feeling a lot of the time.<br /><br />Recommended if you like Sting and have patience for his grander visions that don't sail up the pop charts.mmended if you like Sting and have patience for his grander visions that don't sail up the pop charts.

B00DJ80VLS|2.0|Dream Theater is a band that I own every studio and live album of! I have had the privilege of seeing them live on numerous occasions, and was never disappointed. I should mention that I was first introduced to the music of this band in the mid-to late 1990s, when a friend of mine (Matt), knowing my love for progressive music lent me his copy of \\"Images and Words\\". I have to say that I enjoyed the material immensely, in terms of the vocals and overall musicianship. What I didn't like about that album was the production. \\"Images and Words\\" sounds dated, because of the drum sound.<br /><br />I should probably state that I am a certified rehabilitation counselor, with a strong background in psychology, and sociology spanning over 15 years.<br /><br />I've always been into sound, and it's a proven fact that people psychologically consciously, or unconsciously link sounds with memories.<br /><br />Upon listening to the new self-titled Dream Theater, I found myself generally enjoying the songs, however throughout a majority of the album I was hearing quite a bit of what sounded like Rush songs. This isn't a problem, as I'm a fan of Rush, and I know that the guys in Dream Theater are as well, but in some places the similarities to the Rush albums \\"Permanent Waves\\", and \\"Moving Pictures\\" were actually scary. Moving through the album, the listener reaches the track \\"Along for the Ride\\", which if you take away Mike Mangini's drumming, it could pass for an alternate version of Emerson, Lake & Palmer's classic track \\"Lucky Man\\". Similarities in this album turn to outright plagiarism with the epic \\"Illumination Theory\\"! While listening to this track, I noticed this orchestral progression, and although it is a beautiful arrangement, I kept hearing something else in my head. I stopped the album after several listens, and thought about the melody I was hearing, and despite this progression being only a small portion of the epic track it doesn't just resemble, but is an exact ripoffof The Electric Light Orchestra's \\"Mission, from their album (A World Record).<br /><br />Dream Theater has always paid homage to their influences in subtle ways before, but the self-titled album is a bit, if not drastically obvious in its use of melodies, and sound in general, which brings me back to the statement I made earlier regarding my background in psychology. As I was listening to Dream Theater's \\"Dream Theater\\", something just didn't sound right, and was reminding me of something else. My conclusion was the production sound. The musicians, as always perform in a stellar manner, from James LaBrie's vocals, which are far superior on this album than on his recent solo release \\"Impermanent Resonance\\", to the performances of Jordan Rudess ,John Petrucci, John Myung, and Mike Mangini. With that said, the album ends up being week on originality, and heavy on its reliance of the \\"Images and Words\\" production sound to give the listener a feeling of comfort that this is the same Dream Theater they fell in love with years ago. If you play the new self-titled album, and any track on \\"Images and Words\\", the production sound is virtually identical. This is actually my biggest gripe with the new album, as I never liked the sound to begin with on \\"Images and Words\\". I could actually overlook the plagiarism that's abundantly apparent throughout the album, if I wasn't listening with such a critical ear, due to the production sound.<br /><br />I do think that the bands prior release \\"A Dramatic Turn Of Events\\" was a far better album, and it is clear that Mike Mangini is a great drummer, but Dream Theater should have taken more time to write their self-titled 2013 album.<br /><br />Founding member and original drummer Mike Portnoy, since leaving Dream Theater following the tour for \\"Black Clouds & Silver Linings\\", has went on to work with members of Deep Purple in the band (Flying Colors), and most recently Portnoy found even more success with (The Winery Dogs). Mike Portnoyhas also been the primary drummer for Neal Morse over the past decade, as well as the progressive rock supergroup Transatlantic!<br /><br />Dream Theater's 2013 self-titled album is good, but not great, and I fear that longtime fans of the band are unconsciously drawing a connection to the \\"Images and Words\\" album, and are therefore rationalizing their opinions of the new album. I'm sorry to say that I would not recommend the new Dream Theater album to anyone!<br /><br />If you're going to purchase a fantastic album, buy The Winery Dogs, Flying Colors, any of the Transatlantic albums, as well as those of Neal Morse. You're guaranteed to hear something fresh and original in those suggestions, as opposed to the new Dream Theater.<br /><br />I'm not an anti-Dream Theater fan, or resentful because Mike Portnoy is no longer with them, I am merely stating that since Portnoy's departure he has performed on some incredible material that dwarfs the new Dream Theater.

0307386171|5.0|McEwan's stunningly written story of a very young couple on their wedding evening is one I could not put down. Flying through the pages, I marveled at McEwan's ability to convey both Florence's and Edward's wildly different fears, views and experience of their slowly evolving physical intimacy. Edward and Florence, so very young, are hampered by the mores of the early 1960s, just before the cultural revolution that rang across the world. Despite the pair's disconnect, I expected the couple would work things out through their love for one another.<br /><br />The pair hurtles down a path, each of them headily driven by their individual youthful inexperience, entangled by their interior worlds and their so very different interpretations of what is happening between them. Their story is a jewel of an example of how it can happen that a well-meaning, loving couple can lose their way.<br /><br />While the story's pivotal event occurs less frequently today than in the past, it provides a launch pad for what made the book both memorable and useful. I've never been obsessed with a white whale or stumbled upon refuge from battle in a cathedral of trees, but I was enlarged by reading Moby Dick and The Red Badge of Courage. And that's one reason I read: to enlarge and deepen my understanding.<br /><br />From that perspective, On Chesil Beach offers something valuable to all but the most enlightened of us. McEwan shows Florence and Edward trapped alone an interior world that shapes how each interprets and misinterprets experience and one another. In our own lives, the rest of us peeking out from our own interior worlds have contributed to miscommunication and sometimes outcomes as devastating as the one Florence and Edward unwittingly create. This book deepens my compassion for people and prompts me to be more attentive to the place from which others may be hearing and experiencing the world.

Aside from sounding like many other songs we've already heard, it's a pretty well-done number. \\"We Go Down\\", however, deviates from the pop formula with a drumstep beat and a hard high-pitched drop that goes double-time the second time around. The vocals are still there, but the party vibe is gone - now it's all about survival.<br /><br />\\"Come & Get It\\" is the first previously released track, coming from the trio's Play Harder remix EP, but it fits right in among the beats and rage-ready dubstep. So much better than the Selena Gomez track of the same title. \\"Enjoy the Ride\\" is a much more progressive pop song, describing exactly how much fun Jahan, Yasmine, and Kris are having in their crazy, crazy lives, and while it sounds once again like so much other pop, there's an uplifting vibe to it, and the lyrics are much more well-written than anything else you hear on the radio.<br />Get Wet cannot be placed into a single genre, nor labeled an entirely electronic album. It is simply this: a look inside the hearts of Jahan, Yasmine, and Kris, together the soul and backbone of Krewella.<br /><br />\\"We Are One\\" starts out similarly to \\"Enjoy\\", but the drop goes much harder - built for banging as loud as possible in the largest room possible. Things change up again on the excellent \\"Dancing with the Devil\\", featuring drums from Travis Barker and guest vocals from Fall Out Boy's Patrick Stump. The vocals are just dissonant enough that it gives the song a rock n' roll edge, and the drums definitely help that edge. The Krew's massive hit \\"Alive\\" comes next, and though it's a good song, it feels a bit as if it was put here as a filler track.<br /><br />However, Krewella tries out a seriously different sound on the chillstep \\"Pass The Love Around\\", and it goes over...moderately well. It doesn't fit too well withinall the heavy beats, but it's a nice break before the absolutely massive hardstyle highlight \\"Ring of Fire\\" drops its four-on-the-floor kicks and dirty bassline. \\"Human\\" brings a bit of an emotional vibe with an acoustic guitar riff and a heavy yet melodic dubstep drop with a power ballad guitar solo.<br /><br />Up next is \\"Killin' It\\", another track from the Play Hard EP, and once again, it feels like a bit of a filler - but it's still a really, really good track. The album wraps up with the Pegboard Nerds collaboration \\"This Is Not The End\\", and it goes out with a dubstep bang. The sisters' voices drive the hard-hitting song along to the finale, still proclaiming that it's not the end.<br /><br />The verdict? Despite one or two filler tracks, and some songs sounding as if they're made for the radio, this record is jam-packed with destructive beats, gorgeous vocals, and some very cool collaborations. Play this one as loud as possible.

B000AJIF4E|5.0|I'm always looking for the best deal in headphones. I have a few that are considered up there- Koss Porta Pros, some Senneheisers, the Grado 125's... and somehow I just found out about these a couple months ago through an article on Wire Cutter, when they named them the best headphone under $150.<br /><br />That was pretty remarkable considering they were almost half that- about $78 on sale when I got 'em here on Amazon. The closed (i.e., sound doesn't leak) design and coiled cord makes them more practical than the Grados. And both the structural design (especially the soft ear pads) and the sound itself (I found the sound of the Sonys less harsh and sibilant). Though the Grados have more 'punch' to the bass and a little more detail overall, I think this is the more balanced, true-to-the-source headphone. It's easy to see why they're the industry standard in recording studios around the world.<br /><br />I almost ended up getting the Audio Technicha ATH-M50, but after reading the Wire Cutter article, I got these instead. And at nearly half the price, I'm glad I did. These aren't a pair of headphones that will &#34;enhance&#34; the music you're listening to (like the M50's) through beefed-up bass; these cans will just give you a detailed, unbiased picture of the source: nothing more; nothing less. To some folks used to that sound,  they might think the Sonys sound &#34;recessed&#34; because their frequency balance is so remarkably flat.<br /><br />In summation: These are cans for music fans who just wanna listen to the music, not the headphones.

B006LSZECO|4.0|*SPOILERS WHEN INDICATED* I give Gone Girl four stars, but on it's own merits it deserves three, and compared to other thrillers out there it deserves five. Confused?<br /><br />You should be. Let me explain.<br /><br />It's really hard for me to give the kind of &#34;thrillers&#34; that come out nowadays any more than an average rating. You know the ones I'm talking about - the James Patterson, John Grisham thrillers with their No 1. Bestseller declarations on the covers and their huge fonts on the spines. Gone Girl was more than that; it was refreshingly above average in every way. A suspenseful plot meets fully-fleshed characters, excellent description and prose and subtle human drama to create a page-turning and haunting read. I feel like I should give it MORE than four stars, but really, if I did that I'd feel like a sellout. Here's why:<br /><br />The ending. The ending of Gone Girl was deeply, deeply unsatisfying. Not to mention rushed, out of focus, jolting, annoying, and unsettling. And don't give me no, &#34;Oh that's how the author intended it&#34; baloney. There will be *SPOILERS* in the next few sentences. Now don't get me wrong, I'm fine with books and films in which the heroes do not get retribution and the villains walk away Scot-free. Take a look at Animal Farm and The Usual Suspects for some instances of that. But the ending HAS. To Be. SATISFYING. And ultimately, having Amy - a ruthless, conniving, scheming, despicable femme fatale - getting her way (in everything) is unsatisfying on every level. Our protagonist Nick (who we alternately love and hate through the course of the narrative) - be screwed over and left in the clutch of one of the most hateable (and I don't mean in a good way, as in Joffrey from Game of Thrones) characters in recent memory. It's not that we feel hate towards her (though we do), it's that we hate hearing her, seeing her, and even reading about her. And worst of all? She gets away without one shred of remorse or punishment. This is not a nice feeling to have, and ultimately, the book falls short when it comes to the ending. *Spoilers end* What should have ended with a brutal impact...ended like the flop of a floundering fish.<br /><br />But hey, let's talk pros: The writing was rich and vivid, with great descriptions, chilly moods, atmosphere, and great characters. Gillian Flynn gets you into the minds of her characters like no one else. It's a pity that through out the entire novel, there is not one supremely likeable or relateable character. The plot was suitably intricate and convoluted, and I just loved the &#34;unreliable narrator&#34; aspect of it all, though I was decieved before reading into believing that Gone Girl was a fast paced mystery. It isn't. The plot is slow-burning, taking a long time to get going, but is always engrossing and somewhat riveting. Don't go into this expecting something you will not get: a fast-paced, action-packed thriller. What you will get is a slow-burning, engrossing, complicated, realistic, and twisted thriller. And that's great on it's own merits, isn't it.<br /><br />So that's my review. Gone Girl gets 4 stars for the suspense and atmosphere, not to mention the ingenious plot and characters, though loses points for the absymal anticlimax, for zero sympathetic characters, and for the long time it takes to get started. But once it gets started...this is one of the most memorable and astonishing works of thriller fiction published in recent memory. And it's over to you, David Fincher. Rosamund Pike and Ben Affleck should knock this out of the park.. B00DJZR46G|4.0|I have eagerly awaited Elton John's new albums since I was a kid. I have gone to several midnight release nights at local record stores. Thanks to digital music, that's no longer necessary. The new music can be \\"auto ripped\\" to my computer. As an added bonus, Amazon.com allowed streaming of \\"The Diving Board\\" a week before it's American release so I have listened to it every day since it became available online.<br /><br />From the first piano notes of \\"Oceans Away\\" and Elton's gentle vocals, it's clear this is going to be a striped-down affair, with Elton's beautiful piano playing front and center. The tinge of melancholy in Bernie Taupin's lyrics on the opener, tell of hanging with the \\"old folks\\" to gain some of their wisdom before they pass away.<br /><br />\\"Oscar Wilde Gets Out\\" picks up the pace with the story of, you guessed it, Oscar Wilde. With just the piano, bass, and drums, Elton (as Taupin's muse) tells the tale of the Irish poet and writer. Again, Taupin's lyrics shine while Elton's keyboard swirls around the story and travels of Wilde's brief life and career.  It's an entertaining tale.<br /><br />\\"Town Called Jubilee\\" finds Elton and Bernie in a Southern mood, with a jaunty little tale backed by some good gospel vocals.  By the end of the song, you feel as though you visited the vividly portrayed town.<br /><br />The first three songs are one of the best opening three tunes of an Elton album in a long time.<br /><br />\\"The Ballad of Blind Tom\\" takes a little darker turn telling the story of a \\"freak\\" who entertains all comers. The strings add some texture to this song and again the piano is right up front in the mix.<br /><br />Next is the first of three short interludes labeled as \\"Dreams\\". These are just throwaways and don't really add to the flow of the album.<br /><br />\\"My Quicksand\\" is a rather depressing song, describing the protagonist's downfall due to \\"foolish notions.\\" It's just Elton and his piano except for some minor percussion during the bridge.<br /><br />Next follows one of the weakest songs on the album, \\"Can't Stay Alone Tonight.\\" It may remind loyal Elton fans of \\"Turn the Lights Out When You Leave\\" from \\"Peachtree Road.\\" It's a rather mundane song. Elton and Bernie are capable of much better.<br /><br />\\"Voyeur\\" is next.  It's a hard song to get a handle on. It's a quieter version of Phil Collin's \\"Thru These Walls\\": a little spooky and disturbing. Maybe it's Taupin's commentary on today's surveillance prevalence.<br /><br />Then comes the gorgeous \\"Home Again\\" which hooked me from the very first listen on Facebook. Maybe it was the beautiful landscape in accompanying the video, which I highly recommend everyone view. But the music and the mood of the lyrics link perfectly. It's the story of the melancholy of a person looking back on how far one travels only to end up longing to go back home again. I have listened to this song dozens of times and have not tired of it. It is certain to become a John/Taupin  classic. The piano playing is wonderful.  Listen to the way Elton phrases \\"or was that just some nightclub singer back in 1963.\\"<br /><br />Up next Elton saunters into \\"Take This Dirty Water\\" a surprisingly successful gospel-tinged roll. I have been critical of Elton in the past for his attempts at gospel, but in this case I think he hits the mark, thanks to combination of the piano, backup vocalists, and handclaps. The song doesn't have a lot to say but it saunters nicely.<br /><br />\\"The New Fever Waltz\\" slows the pace down, talking about \\"too much war, too little love\\" and the innocence of the dance before battle. The piano solo in the break is beautiful, supplemented by a gentle horn section.<br /><br />\\"Mexican Vacation\\" took a few listens to grow on for me. The live version from the Columbia session really helped me take to the song. Elton's piano is superb throughout and the tune really swings.<br /><br />Last comes the title song, \\"The Diving Board\\" a surprisingly dull finale. Themetaphor doesn't work for me, but maybe other listeners will relate.<br /><br />I was not thrilled when I heard T-Bone Burnett was producing this album. I am not a fan of his stripped down, organic production. I think several of the songs on Elton's previous album \\"The Union\\" (with Leon Russell) could have been better with a different producer. But I think Burnett did OK with this effort. Minimal instruments and add-ons really allow Elton to make this album the piano album he has been promising fans for years. I hope his existing fans and new fans give this album a few listens. I give it a B+ and recommend it.
B00CA4S27W|4.0|This is another good effort from Blackmore's Night. No surprises here and in many ways more of the same from this group. Over the past several years they have carved out a nice little niche with their modern spin on &#34;Renaissance Music&#34;. Their sound is a blending of old world music meets modern instruments. Candice's voice is a delight to listen to and she delivers again with this set. Richie's guitar and other string work is excellent as always. The songs are very much in keeping with their past efforts. However, none of them really grabbed me. I guess I am always looking for that special something in a song that strike a cord with my soul. Those songs are few and far between and while the tracks on this album are good, none of them reach that level. If you're a fan you'll enjoy this album. If you are new to their music, this is a good representation of what they do so well.

0345528581|3.0|Hundreds of 5 star reviews should make anyone suspicious in this category. This is not, and never will be a classic.<br /><br />The good:<br /><br />The only part of the book that is really good is the actual descriptions of exercises, and this bumped an otherwise 1 star book up to 3 stars, since they are the main reason I bought the book. The exercises are pretty much in order of difficulty within muscle groups, with very good descriptions and clear photos. I started doing strength training a couple months ago, and was looking for a reference of bodyweight exercises I could use to vary and scale up my workouts. This book supplies plenty of material, some of which is so difficult I will probably never be able to do it, and plenty more that is at or near my level. Some of the exercises involve props, like heavy boxes, chairs, or doors, but nothing that people don't commonly have around the house. That said, I'm looking into making a sandbag or something else cheap and heavy instead of trying to use a backpack or box of books, and the only door I'd trust my weight to when hanging off the top is the door to the outside.  This section could be improved with descriptions of what poor form looks like, what the most common form errors are, and more pictures of some of the advanced exercises. It could also be improved changing the format of how variations are listed to make it clear they are variations, and why making a certain change increases or decreases the difficulty. It is often, but not always obvious. But since the book is cheap, this section is still worth 5 stars.<br /><br />The rest of the book falls way short.<br /><br />The indifferent:<br /><br />The sample workouts aren't very useful to me, and neither is the section on how to build a workout. The samples are not a standard workout program (3-4 days a week, x number of sets and reps), such as I was looking for simply because it is proven, easy to remember, and easy to carry out, and for a beginner any programis novel. Instead, he tries to make it `interesting', even at the beginning level. Instead of a set number of reps, he wants you to do `Ladders', which is a variation he describes earlier in the book. They don't sound like a bad way to gain strength, but it's more complicated than saying do the exercise x number of times, adjusting x or the exercise as your strength grows, and he gives no evidence as to whether his ideas are more or less effective than standard sets of reps. He also has 5 days a week of working out, which is a lot (some days hard, some easier). His sample workout is designed to get you into boot camp style shape, but that is not everyone's goal, and he does not provide detailed information on how to scale down for people who can't handle that much, or simply don't need that level of result, and don't want to put in that much work.<br /><br />He has a little information on how to design your own program, but it isn't well structured, and again, for a beginner who doesn't know what they are doing, it lacks detail. I ended up using the Ultimate Weight Training Workout Routine on an outside website to figure out what a good strength program should include, plus this book to pick which exercises.<br /><br />He's also got a chapter on nutrition. Take it for what it is- a guy who is in really good shape, and eats fairly well is telling you what works for him. It may work for you, it may not. It doesn't add anything to the book's value.<br /><br />The bad:<br /><br />The book's introductory chapters were almost enough to turn me off completely. He writes about his background, trying to prove his credentials. A one paragraph About the Author section would have done the same job. I was pretty indifferent to his life story (yes, you're clearly a macho man, now get over yourself), but then it goes downhill. He's got a bunch of bull about how bodyweight is better than free weights, and therefore everyone should do it, but doesn't bother with actual evidence. Personally, I use it because it's cheap, and can be done anywhere. That's one of his arguments, but he also gives the hilarious example that no one ever lies on their back to lift things, the way a bench press has you do. Later in the book, he extols the pushup. Personally, I've never tried picking up heavy things while lying on my face. Promoting your chosen method of gaining strength is one thing. Pretending another proven method is illegitimate just makes you sound stupid, especially if you don't bother with science or even logic to back up your personal biases.<br /><br />Minor point. Something common to every strength training book I've read is that they are written for men. They usually include a few pages about how women can and should train almost exactly the same as men, and in this one half the pictures are of a woman, but the prose is aimed towards men who want to look big and manly, and lift heavy things like a manly man can. Not worth a star, but definitely enough to make me roll my eyes at some points.<br /><br />Overall: The list and description of exercises earn this book a legitimate place on my shelf. If I ever run out of shelf space, I can always tear out the other half of the book.

B00DJ80VLS|5.0|Published with permission from MusicPlayers.com, the online magazine for serious musicians:<br /><br />If you're one of the skeptics wondering what was to become of Dream Theater in the post-Portnoy years, fear not. On the aptly self-titled album, Dream Theater, the band reminds everyone why they are the most beloved band in the prog metal genre. This is an album true to their name, and one that deftly combines heavy metal with progressive rock and classic hard rock. It's full of orchestral movements, extraordinary musicianship, loads of rich melodies and powerful rock content. It paints a picture; it tells a story.<br /><br />We knew that bringing Mike Mangini into the band lineup was going to really take things to another place once he became part of the songwriting process--the drum parts for A Dramatic Turn of Events were already written when he joined the band in 2011. Sure enough, the drumming here is sure to dazzle and impress. There's plenty of double-kick work to keep metalheads pumping their fists, but it's all the other grace and groove that Mangini brings that creates a subtle shift in the vibe of the music and takes it to places slightly new.<br /><br />Two of our favorite tracks,\\"The Looking Glass\\" and \\"Surrender to Reason\\" pay obvious progressive rock homages to Rush. In fact, there are multiple songs on Dream Theater that clock in under six minutes. But we were drawn in right from the orchestral opening and demonically tight and heavy guitars of \\"False Awakening Suite\\" and left in awe by the album closing, twenty-two minute epic, \\"Illumination Theory.\\"<br /><br />John Petrucci's guitar work is stellar as usual, as is the keyboard work of Jordan Rudess and the bass work of John Myung. There are plenty of subtly different guitar tones on display here for the tone obsessed (yes, it's all still obviously Mesa tone), and Rudess' chops are dazzling as ever, and share space with some great orchestra performances in the album opening and closing tracks.<br /><br />Myung is on fire. Not only did he contribute lyrics to a song (die hards look for this little detail), but you'll hear him soloing (along with other bandmates) on the instrumental track, \\"Enigma Machine.\\" Yes, you heard it, sports fans. It's the return of the instrumental, and it rips, complete with dueling soloing lines like only this band can deliver.<br /><br />And what of our dear friend, James LaBrie? Fantastic job with the vocals here. I think the work he's done on his two recent solo albums (check out his fantastic new release, Impermanent Resonance) has influenced his vocal contributions here, as he's sounding really melodic, sometimes with a big rock voice, as well as delivering some nice intimate moments set against acoustic guitar backdrops. Favorites would have to include the memorable, \\"Along for the Ride,\\" with a vocal hook that will stick in your head like a classic `70s rock song (not to mention the vocals are followed by a very Keith Emerson-like synth solo).<br /><br />Enough of my babbling. There just isn't any weak spot on Dream Theater. We love this release. This is Dream Theater sounding better than ever. If you were a rabid fan of the band circa Images & Words, Awake, and Falling into Infinity, you'll find this album to be more of a return to form, but combined with their updated, modern metal edge. And once again, we're thrilled that overly aggressive mastering didn't kill this release like far too many metal genre records today.<br /><br />-- SK<br /><br />(to read this and other reviews, please visit MusicPlayers.com)

The denouement is the result of a deathbed confession, and surprises all the characters. So on the basic level of a 'whodunit' it fails miserably.<br /><br />But for a true Austen fan, the worse problem is James' ham-handed attempt to sound like Austen. She uses old-style prose, but has none of the wit or sensitivity of Austen; her plot is terribly thin and its development is repetitive and redundant; and the end result bored me to death and irritated me. Additionally, she turns some of our favorite characters (Elizabeth and Jane Bennett, Darcy and Bingley, even Lydia and Wickham) into one-dimensional drones with not a single interesting speech between them. If the sparkle and charm of 'Pride and Prejudice' are like an ice-cold glass of the finest champagne, 'Death at Pemberley' is like trying to swallow a giant cup of mud.<br /><br />In short, if you love Austen, don't waste your time on this mess. Instead, read the Adam Dalgleish books that James actually excels at.

0307271609|5.0|Jung Chang has written a scholarly, readable, and vastly interesting biography of Empress Dowager Cixi who ruled China for over four decades in the late 19th century. This remarkable woman spent her life trying to modernize and improve the lives of the Chinese people. According to the author, Cixi \\"brought in modernity to replace decrepitude, poverty, and savagery and absolute power and she introduced hitherto untasted humaneness, open-mindedness and freedom.\\" This book details her struggles and accomplishments. Cixi was chiefly responsible for China's entrance into the modern world by instituting policies that built railways, telecommunications networks, modern shipping, and other infrastructures. She introduced educational and cultural reforms that erased China's xenophobic views of the world. I agree with the author that \\"one cannot but admire this amazing stateswoman, flawed though she was.\\"<br />Empress Dowager Cixi not only details Cixi's accomplishments but it also describes China's culture of tradition and servitude. B00DR0PDNE|4.0|The device is great if you use Google products (movies from Google Play) and watch lots of YouTube. Otherwise it can be a disappointment.<br /><br />The Chromecast device streams wirelessly from your device to the TV. The downside is that if you have Amazon Prime the device is unusable unless you stream from a laptop or desktop. Using a laptop or desktop with Google Chrome browser you can stream anything to the TV but you lose clarity. I believe it streams at 720 vs full 1080.<br /><br />Chromecast I believe was designed to better monetize Google products. Example, to stream a movie, you can stream via Google Play vs. Amazon or other movie providers where it won't work on a mobile device. For me, I have a desktop with a TV a few feet away. I can &#34;cast&#34; via my Google browser. But if I go downstairs with my Xoom or iPad, then I'm stuck with YouTube or movies from Google Play, which I don't believe offer any freebies.<br /><br />Lastly, signal strength. The Roku has better signal strength. I tried both in a back bedroom with a weak WIFI signal. Chromecast cannot pick up the signal. The Roku can. As an FYI, the Chromecast works as follows --- when you click on a URL in say YouTube, Chromecast is sending the URL to your router and receiving the signal, thus the 1080 playback and better signal. When you click on a URL using the browser and a desktop then the call is made to the router but the video is streamed from desktop to TV, thus 720 playback.<br /><br />I understand why Google created this. I don't blame them. Just understand the limitations. It would be easy for this device to &#34;cast&#34; any URL but that defeats Google's purpose of monetizing their assets. Hopefully someone can come along and provide a low cost device that can stream content wirelessly from the Net.
